<user>111785770370296789381< /user>< user_name>
Jay Hussein (Jayzakh)</user_name>
< Time>
1510340455396< /Time>
<Rate>5<//Rate>< Text>
Came here twice, first time I loved it and second time? Still LOVED it!
Parking is pretty easy to find and the whole restaurant exterior is painted light green so you can't miss it! It's all halal and I was intrigued by the menu.

The seating is either in front or in the back patio which is fully covered yet still outside. Fells really nice. Really cozy setting kind of like a sun room!
There are booth like seating across the wall around the room.

Ordered the potato chips, homemade sauce platter, beef kabob and beef and cheese gozleme.

The potato chips are homemade, freshly made so they come out piping hot. They are crispy and soft at the same time! Would recommend this appetizer!

The homemade sauce platter was amazing. The green is a mint sauce, the white is a creamy yogurt sauce and of course the red is a spicy chili sauce. If you can't defeat the heat then do not eat the spicy sauce or you might not be around for the rest of your order. My favorite was the yogurt sauce by far. Ask for some extra yogurt because it goes amazing with your kabob!

The kabob was good. Standard beef Angus kabob. It was decent but then again you can get kabobs everywhere honestly.

Now for the Gozleme! THIS was something different!!! Usually the beef comes by itself but add cheese in there! They come in three large tortillas which are not really tortillas but the best way to describe it. The cheese is kinda sweet which meshes in well with the beef! By far my favorite dish here as I've ordered it twice!

Will be returning here soon whenever I'm down here, until then stay spicy my friends (or not)< /Text>

<Rating>4< /Rating><user_id>103341861700586354001< /user_id><Time>1500675070932<//Time><user_name>Jonathan Lee< /user_name>< text>
I had been itching to try Yuchun for a while and finally got around to it. You're going to Yuchun for their cold noodle dishes, most likely for the mul naengmyeon (a cold, tangy, sweet beef broth surrounding chewy noodles that Yuchun makes with kudzu). I think I slightly prefer the milmyeon at Hangari Bajirak for cold broth noodles, but Yuchun is damn fine.

This is a newer location than the one on Olympic, which is reflected in the newer, shinier environs. Parking is still a major headache, though. Either drive around hoping to find something at a meter, or chance the overcrowded valet parking lot.< /text>

< Review>
Though my experience at Jane at the Marketplace has been mostly positive, today in celebration of my sister's birthday...I have a few exceptions.
First of all I must say that our server, Catherine did a very good job. She was cheery, and informative. Ditto the dude in charge running the front end.
I have always liked the environment here: big space, cloth napery and good quality glass and cutlery. A mid priced  restaurant with the class to fill the space with touches that make a difference in our overall enjoyment.
There were 4 of us today and we ordered:
Med Pizza
Blackened plank Salmon with french fries and Mango/Citrus coulis
Turkey Cobb with Gorgonzola
Red Onion Rings
Coconut Cake
Last time here i ordered the (i assume) Special Pizza which was a pretty spectacular Prosciutto, Mushrooms on a white, cheese sauce. A very delicious item. (i've attached a photo of this pizza to this review along with the Med pizza)
This Med Pizza was a major disappointment. The crust was lifeless and tasteless and was an odd tan color: as it it were whole wheat which it doesn't seem to be based on the menu description. Something was off with this dough: not leavened enough? Leavened too much?
The Buffalo Mozz was good but there just wasn't enough Olive tapenade to make an impression. Worst of all, the greens were dry when they should have been dressed. Even dressed with just olive oil, salt and pepper. Where was the Balsamic?
My sister very much enjoyed the Salmon and found the Mango/Citrus  sauce a tasty accompaniment to the fish. The Salmon was of excellent quality and grilled as ordered. A very good dish.
The Turkey Cobb was good: all of the accoutrements were prepared very well though the Gorgonzola pieces were ridiculously big. Odd to be sure. Also the Turkey was good: obviously not deli turkey but either bought or cooked in house. The greens were crispy and fresh.
The Firestone Red Onion Rings are once again pretty perfect: light, well seasoned batter but also fried very very well. This item is a prime example of a simple dish elevated to ultra goodness because all of the pieces are handled with care and in a careful, thoughtful manner.
The Coconut Cake arrived with a candle which was unlit and no one from the staff to sing Happy Birthday. Huh? a 200 buck lunch ($50 check average for each of us 4) and no one could spare the time?
Despite that, this cake is as coco-nutty as you can get. The cake itself was tender, fluffy and redolent of coconut . Both the buttercream and filling were delicious. The portion of cake sits in a milk-style sauce jam packed with coconut flavor. No artificial coconut "extracts" in sight or in the taste of this cake!
I can see  why people love this item.<//Review>

Ive been to this restaurant twice and my experience was wonderful both times. On this visit, I ordered the Grilled Chicken plate for dinner. It was absolutely delicious. It had a light cream sauce that was delicate and complimented the Anaheim chiles and chicken. The roasted potato side had so much flavor, I could have easily eaten 10 more servings. 1)  WAY TOO EXPENSIVE!!  We usually stay at Motel 6 for budgeting reasons ... this time, the prices were just too high!  Even though there is an event in town, the prices shouldn't be hiked up so very much!

<gmap_id>0x80ecf0ce8f23c2cf:0x9829ede04ee2907d<//gmap_id>< text>
The front desk staff were very friendly and accommodating, but that's where the good ends. The price was $113 for a Saturday night stay booked in advance - that's expensive for a motel, but super expensive for how dirty and uncomfortable this room was.

The room was neatly made up, but it had clearly not been cleaned properly. The floor was disgustingly dirty - we didn't realize just how bad it was until we took our shoes and socks off to shower (picture attached) - the hardwood floor felt like it hadn't been swept or mopped in months.

The shower was dirty, with hair in the drain and recent dirt stains (not the permanent kind, the kind you can wipe off with a rag). The towels had multiple stains and were so rough it was clear their usefulness as towels had long passed.

There was a roach under my son's bed - roaches don't bother me that much, but they really bothered my young son, who almost didn't want to sleep in the room any more. That was a hassle I definitely didn't want to deal with.

The parking lot had a lot of trash and debris and the pool area looked like it hadn't been cleaned in awhile.

Finally, they offered kids lollipops in the registration office, but I took a look at the container and the lollipops all looked like they had had their wrappers removed and then re-wrapped. One of them was put back in with no wrapper at all! (picture attached).

Overall, this Motel 6 is much dirtier and more uncomfortable to stay in that most Motel 6s I've been in, especially when you consider it's in San Luis Obispo, which is a beautiful town. Not worth the money. Spend another $20 or $30 and book at an actual hotel.</text>

I had a wonderful stay at Motel 6 in San Luis Obispo (North); the amenities were basic but clean, and the rooms were serviced every day and kept very neat by the housekeeping staff.

What made this stay so memorable however, was Jeramie Gaines going ABOVE AND BEYOND.
